Special Issue for the Relocation and Opening of the Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company's Head Office

An Abbreviated History and Remarks of the Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company's Shanghai General Distribution Office 188

The Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company was established in the late years of the Guangxu reign of the former Qing Dynasty, pioneering the cigarette industry in our country. Subsequently, many followed suit, but the scale and vision of the former remains unmatched to this day. The head office is located in Shanghai, with branches in various provinces of China, as well as Hong Kong, Java, Surabaya, Batavia, Singapore, and Siam in Nanyang. Factories were established in Shanghai, Hong Kong, Hankou, and Liaoning, employing a total of 20,000 to 30,000 male and female workers. The annual output is approximately 200,000 large cases, with a business value of approximately 30 to 40 million national currency. The company bears approximately 10 million yuan in national unified taxes, significantly impacting the national economy and people's livelihood. Its history and glory are well-known to Chinese scholars discussing the domestic tobacco industry. Today, as the Shanghai General Distribution Office of the company moves to its new location at No. 25 Guizhou Road and holds its opening ceremony, we further inform the people of the country about the evolution and history of the General Distribution Office. Tracing back to the emergence of domestically produced cigarettes in Shanghai, the ten-cigarette pack of "Flying Boat" brand from the Nanyang Tobacco Company was the pioneer. However, at that time, only Guangdong food stores in the Hongkou and Wuchang Road areas occasionally sold it, as the cigarettes were manufactured in Hong Kong and only brought over in small quantities by sailors on ships between Hong Kong and Shanghai. Smokers and vendors could not obtain them in large quantities. In the third year of the Republic of China, Mr. Chen Caibao, a member of the cigarette industry, recognizing the significant annual outflow of funds due to imported cigarettes in Shanghai, united with more than ten local businesses, including Kaitai, Xiangdelong, Changdelong, Dasheng, Tongyoufeng, Chen Wanfeng, Xiefeng, Yongfeng, and Shaotongyu, to pool capital and establish a distribution office. This office directly ordered goods from the Nanyang Head Office in Hong Kong and transported them to Shanghai to compete with imported products. Within a few months, sales gradually increased, and this distribution office became the precursor to today's General Distribution Office. At that time, Mr. Jian Zhaonan, the founder and general manager of the Nanyang Head Office, was planning to establish a branch in Shanghai as the first step in developing the domestic tobacco market in Central and Northern China. In the fourth year of the Republic of China, a location was found at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Guangxi Road (now the address of the Henderley Clock and Watch General Store) to establish the Shanghai Nanyang Tobacco Company. A manufacturing plant was also planned at the intersection of Broadway Road and Zhaofeng Road. The cigarettes sold along the coast could be supplied by the Shanghai factory, benefiting both manufacturing and sales. The distribution part of the business was actually under the Shanghai branch. These events occurred between the fifth, sixth, and seventh years of the Republic of China. By the eighth year, the company was fully expanded and reorganized. The head office was moved to Shanghai, choosing another location at No. 12 Nanjing Road, while the original location at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Guangxi Road became the Shanghai Distribution Office, responsible for business in Shanghai. In the tenth year, a distribution office was established on North Sichuan Road in Hongkou, called the North Distribution Office. The one at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Guangxi Road was called the South Distribution Office, with the Wusong River and Suzhou River as the boundary, managing business affairs in the north and south of Shanghai respectively. In the eleventh year, the North Distribution Office was merged into the South Distribution Office. Thus, the name "General Distribution Office" was officially established. From the twelfth to the twenty-second year of the Republic of China, the General Distribution Office was renamed "Shanghai Bureau" twice, referred to as the "Bureau System," once renamed "Shanghai Baosongtai Section," referred to as the "Section System," and once changed to "Xintaihe Agency," referred to as the "General Agency System." Its address moved once to No. 16 Yuanyuan Lane on Tianjin Road, then to No. 399 Songshou Lane on Beijing Road, and then to Zhengjia Wood Bridge on Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession. The initial heads were Li Jingsuo, Jian Yinchu, and Hu Zijin, followed by Chen Caibin, Rong Yaoqu, Sun Lishan, Zhao Zuyi, Jiang Zhengqing, and Huang Jieheng. From the twenty-second year of the Republic of China to the present, Mr. Wu Dingju has been appointed, with Wei Ronghui and Wu Jingshan assisting him. The above is the past history of the General Distribution Office over the past decade, generally adapting to the environment and trends of the time. The employees, retailers, and the company have formed an inseparable bond. With long experience, they have gained more expertise, and with long-term cooperation, their feelings have become closer. Therefore, the products of the Nanyang Tobacco Company are becoming increasingly refined, and the sales of the Nanyang Tobacco Company are improving daily. This can be seen from the General Distribution Office, which is not achieved by chance. Shanghai is the hub of national commerce and a pioneer in the flow of goods. Any new product, whether foreign or domestic, must be sold in Shanghai before it can be sold throughout the country. In the cigarette industry, the government also designated Shanghai as the location for manufacturing plants, ahead of Tianjin, Hankou, and Qingdao. When the Nanyang Company arrived in Shanghai, foreign cigarettes already had a dominant position. The Nanyang Company reclaimed a place in the market through hard work and struggle. Before branch offices and warehouses could be established in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Shandong, Hebei, Hubei, Jiangxi, and even the three northeastern provinces, they all relied on the General Distribution Office for support. At the peak of domestic cigarette factories in Shanghai, there were about 150 to 160 factories. However, they were subsequently suppressed by foreign goods dumping and tax system restrictions, and only 30 to 40 factories remain today. The Nanyang Company has worked hard to support and fight tirelessly. In Shanghai, the General Distribution Office has put in the most effort and achieved the most significant results. Every new trademark launched by the Nanyang Company has been promoted and launched by the General Distribution Office. There are over a hundred types, all with outstanding reputations. People in the north and south are accustomed to smoking them, and they are ingrained in their minds, often making it impossible to switch to other brands. Notable examples include Little and Big White Gold Dragon, Mei Lanfang, Seven Stars, Little and Big Great Wall, Linked Beads, Patriotic, Red Gold Dragon, Hundred Birds, Happy Birds, High Tower, Crab Beauty, Golden Axe, and Eight Corners, which are popular products throughout the north and south. Recently, the ten-pack Red Gold Dragon in Shanghai has adapted to social needs, offering affordable prices and good quality, with almost every household having them. The General Distribution Office's relocation includes the distribution of top-quality fifty-pack and ten-pack Big White Gold Dragon cigarettes with special discount coupons to thank the people for their welcome and support. Its sales have recently extended overseas, spreading rapidly without promotion, which is unmatched by other cigarettes. The internal organization of the General Distribution Office is similar to that of branch offices in various regions, but its position in Shanghai is particularly important. Initially, it only managed business within a hundred miles of Shanghai. Last year, it also managed Hangzhou, Jiaxing, Huzhou, and Shaoxing in Zhejiang Province. This year, it also manages the four warehouses in Suzhou, Wuxi, Zhenjiang, and Xinpu. Furthermore, merchants from Xinjiang, Guizhou, and other provinces who purchase and sell goods locally are also attached to it. With long journeys and distant management, its affairs are becoming increasingly complex. Mr. Wu Dingju, the current head, has been working at the Nanyang Company for over ten years. He trained in the Shanghai West and Pudong factories for several years. Every year, the company sends personnel to Shandong and Henan to purchase tobacco leaves, and he often participates in this task. He has also managed the Hangzhou office for several years. He has extensive experience in manufacturing and business, both in theory and practice. With the assistance of Mr. Wei Ronghui and Mr. Wu Jingshan, the business of the General Distribution Office will surely prosper even more. The General Manager of the Nanyang Company, Mr. Jian Yujie, can be said to be thorough and appropriate in his selection of personnel. In recent years, all industries have declined, and the business community has fallen into a state of depression. Foreign goods have attacked, and Shanghai is at the forefront of this. The domestic cigarette business is currently facing one of its most serious and difficult days. In addition, the country is in crisis, and the domestic market is flooded with illicit cigarettes. Small stalls along the remote roads of the concessions sell hand-rolled cigarettes, relying on impoverished livelihoods, which the government is unable to control. They evade national taxes and counterfeit trademarks, without exception. However, the rolling paper used for these so-called illicit cigarettes and hand-rolled cigarettes is reportedly smuggled by a certain foreigner, who also prints brand names to supply them. Even in the small matter of a cigarette, people use all kinds of tricks to scheme against us, like mercury seeping into every crevice. The national economy and people's livelihood are significantly affected, which is further proof. We hope that fellow members of the domestic cigarette industry and those who purchase domestic cigarettes will pay attention to this quickly. This is not just the loss of one company or the responsibility of one or two individuals.

Advocating for Domestic Cigarettes 190

— Zhang Jinglu

I have often heard that treading on frost leads to solid ice, and accumulated water can erode stone. Calamities easily arise from neglect, and changes often occur unexpectedly. Minor ailments can affect the heart, and a gentle breeze can spread across the universe. One should not neglect things simply because they seem small or insignificant. Cigarettes are extremely fine and insignificant, and the world generally considers them trivial, with the lingering fragrance and fleeting smoke having no connection to grand principles. However, one should know that foreign cigarettes are sold throughout the country, with deep-rooted habits reaching rural areas. The money spent by Chinese people on these cigarettes flows overseas like smoke, amounting to hundreds of millions each year, which is beyond the consideration of the general public. It is truly frightening how a small spark can start a prairie fire, and how a trickle, if not stopped, will become a river!

The Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company is the pioneer of self-made cigarettes in our country and a giant in the Chinese cigarette industry. The excellence of its products and the grandeur of its scale are enough to surpass foreign merchants, turning foreign products into dung. Those who monopolize and profiteer are forced to stand cautiously, watching with sideways glances, feeling like they are sitting on pins and needles and have thorns in their backs, no longer able to snore peacefully in their beds. This is something that our country, facing many difficulties and lagging behind in many aspects, should take as a source of consolation.

Some may argue that cigarettes merely cause Chinese people to waste huge sums of money each year and are merely a consumption product with no need for advocacy or encouragement. Moreover, at a time when we are surrounded by enemies and hanging by a thread, we should vigorously practice new lifestyle disciplines, without懈怠or弛懈. Why waste useful money on useless extravagance? This argument is indeed startling and makes sense. However, if we consider the facts, if we could get all Chinese people to abstain from cigarettes, that would be fine. But if that is not the case, should we simply watch people send hundreds of millions of dollars away each year and remain indifferent? If this continues, others will become richer while we become poorer, others will be the knife and chopping board while we are the fish and meat. This is precisely why ambitious people feel慷慨 and忧伤, and think day and night about挽回利权 and杜塞漏巵in every possible way. Therefore, the establishment of the Nanyang Tobacco Company is to meet the needs of the Chinese people and cultivate the vitality of the nation, and it is something that cannot be dispensed with or delayed!

My personal opinion is that if foreign cigarettes are not eliminated from the market, then domestic cigarettes must be promoted to resist them. It is best for Chinese people not to smoke cigarettes at all, but if they do, they must choose domestic products over foreign ones. To take back what was lost, to mend the fold after the sheep is lost, is a second-best option. As for its ability to aid literary thoughts and dispel worries, that is just a minor benefit.

Now that the Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company's General Distribution Office is moving to a new location, a special publication will be compiled in commemoration. I express my views frankly here, not only because I appreciate it as a wonderful companion for tea and after-dinner drinks, but also because I am happy that it can be a sharp tool for杜塞漏巵.

Thoughts on the Relocation and Opening of the Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company General Distribution Office 191

Running a business is like building a nation. Those who succeed possess patriotism and love for the people, along with unique insights and unwavering courage. I deeply admire the Jian brothers for establishing the Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company.

Merchants typically pursue profit, but perceptions of profit vary. Some have a broad vision, while others have a narrow one. Such differences in perspective are undeniable. Chinese merchants often share a negative habit: when one starts a business, others rush to imitate it. Soon, everyone joins the competition, even resorting to mimicking brand names and trademarks, disregarding ethics and laws. Such actions lead to mutual destruction and collapse. Even if they follow established paths, their gains remain minimal. This reflects a narrow perspective. A broader vision is different.

The cigarette industry originated with foreign merchants. People embraced cigarettes for their convenience, leading to their rapid popularity. Traditional Chinese tobacco products, like water pipes, gradually declined. Merchants in those industries failed to unite and innovate. Few visionary leaders emerged to challenge foreign companies. This allowed foreign cigarette companies to seize our profits and grow stronger. This is a painful example of the shallowness of Chinese merchants. The Jian brothers were different.

The Jian brothers possessed patriotism and love for the people. They used foreign capital to revitalize domestic commerce. Their vision and insight were exceptional. When the Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company began in Shanghai, China was boycotting foreign goods. To succeed, domestic goods needed to compete with foreign products, requiring sufficient resources. Understanding this, the Jians worked tirelessly, increasing capital and improving product quality. Despite facing setbacks, they persevered and succeeded in challenging foreign dominance.

The rise of the Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company also spurred the emergence of other Chinese cigarette companies. The Chinese cigarette industry thrived, gradually diminishing the influence of foreign companies.

Before the Nanyang Company, foreign companies dominated the market, reaping enormous profits. Although some taxes were paid, the state's revenue remained minimal. With the rise of Nanyang, cigarette taxes steadily increased. Chinese merchants eagerly paid taxes, and foreign companies followed suit. Before the Republic, cigarette tax revenue was insignificant. Now, cigarette taxes contribute significantly to the national treasury. Besides the government, countless workers and merchants benefit directly or indirectly. Generous donations were also made to education, disaster relief, and cultural causes. This exemplifies the embodiment of patriotism and love for the people. The Jian brothers are truly giants in the business world. This essay commemorates the relocation of the Nanyang Company's General Distribution Office and expresses my personal views.

Human Life and Cigarettes 193

— Rongfang

In terms of material consumption, the mainstays of human life are food, cotton cloth, and silk. In terms of spiritual consumption, they are culture, faith, and art. When combined, these two aspects propel human life towards a higher stage – sophistication. As such, we cannot neglect either of them.

Plain cotton cloth represents pure material, untouched by spiritual influence. However, once it is woven with patterns or printed with designs, it becomes beautiful and appealing. It then fulfills the dual needs of human life, making it appealing to mischievous younger siblings. Similarly, plain wheat flour, when simply made into solid buns, represents a product devoid of spiritual power. However, when skilled chefs use their artistic flair to create a variety of elaborate pastries, they cater to the palates of young ladies and gentlemen. From this, we can infer that spiritual and material aspects are equally important in human life – although some occasionally prioritize spiritual life over material, even willing to consume coarse rice in order to accommodate their higher beliefs. This we can only归纳到别一问题上去说了.

Considering the dual needs of human life reminds us of cigarettes. While some may see cigarettes as meaningless consumables, they are in fact a unique product that combines material and spiritual aspects in the context of human life. While we certainly cannot subsist solely on cigarettes all day long, they are an indispensable necessity in the appropriate time and context. One needs only to pay a little attention in various settings to understand that there is a solid theoretical foundation behind their existence.

Cigarettes can be divided into domestic and foreign varieties, but in reality, there is no difference. Those who believe foreign cigarettes are superior to domestic ones likely subscribe to the notion that the foreign moon is brighter than the Chinese one.

Among the manufacturers of domestic cigarettes, Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company is widely recognized as the most reputable and historically significant in China. Therefore, their products, regardless of quality or packaging, surpass ordinary cigarettes, as everyone imagines.

The Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company was established in Shanghai and Hong Kong, with branch offices set up throughout the country. If not for the Chinese people's protection of domestic goods and concerted efforts, how could this have been achieved? All of us Chinese people should strengthen our ambitions, work together to achieve strength for our country, and block漏巵in the economic flow. Therefore, every person is responsible for the rise and fall of the country, and promoting domestic goods is also a way to save the nation, a small responsibility that we people are still unable to carry out. If we abandon our writing brushes and join the army, guarding the country with weapons, there will be no 纶矣. At this critical moment of survival, I hope that we will shoulder and carry out our responsibility to save the country through domestic goods.

Night Ramblings 196

— Chen Mingzhang

(Collected from the brand names of Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company)

"Great Happiness" indeed came as promised, along with her two younger sisters, "Double Happiness" and "Four Happiness", hand-in-hand, approaching gracefully. Smiles bloomed on my face, and I rushed to greet them, wanting to make my beloved feel satisfied and happy. I flattered them, saying like a toady, "The weather is very clear tonight, how about we go to a more distant place to play?" Fortunately, the three sisters favored me, and agreed without hesitation. Moreover, I could tell from their expressions that they were very happy and interested, which made me even more delighted. I quickly made a phone call to the "Airplane" field in Longhua, instructing them to release an "Airship", and we flew high above the "Earth".

In the sky, we enjoyed the scenery above the clouds. Because it was around the Mid-Autumn Festival, the moon was particularly "Bright." Looking closely, we could vaguely see two "Brothers" inside, wielding a "Golden Axe" to chop down a large tree, with a large "Cat" lying beside them, enjoying the spectacle. Suddenly, with a thunderous sound in the sky, fifty large "Platinum Dragon" cigarettes and ten small "Platinum Dragon" cigarettes flew over, along with "Red Golden Dragon" cigarettes, bulging their eyes and opening their mouths in a state of wanting to devour us. We were all extremely frightened, so scared that we dared not move. We just urged the pilot to drive faster. I secretly thought to myself, the Heavenly Palace must be afraid that we would "Leak Heavenly Secrets" (?).

The "Airship" flew very fast, and in a blink of an eye, we arrived in North China. The "Great Wall" and "Small Wall" lay coiled like snakes, big and small, on the high mountains. On the mountains were "High Towers" and "Pagodas" standing tall into the clouds. Inside the towers, they were performing Peking Opera, "The Cowherd and Weaver Girl Meeting on the Magpie Bridge", with "Magpies" that could transform into a bridge, "Seven Stars" lanterns, and "Mei Lanfang's" authentic billboard. There were many people watching. Tickets only cost "Thirty Cents" and "Eighty Cents", two types.

Flying past the Great Wall and heading east, passing through Shenyang, Changchun and other places, we arrived at Changbai Mountain, where ginseng is produced. At the foot of the mountain, we saw several "Hundred Birds" and "Golden Deer" running back and forth. The summit was precipitous, and at the highest point stood a "Flower Queen", said to be transformed from a "Beauty," so the flowers that bloomed were also very delicate and beautiful.

Because I still had to go to the "Bank" as usual to work tomorrow morning, I instructed the driver to return by the original route.

As soon as I stepped off the airship, I felt dizzy and disoriented. I bought a box of "Small Linked Pearls" cigarettes at a nearby cigarette shop and shared them with everyone.

This trip to North China indeed wasted a night, but what I gained was also good, making me deeply feel that North China is indeed a "Rich Country". However, the landscape remains the same, but the people are all different. How will the "Patriotic" youths take it back and complete the "Unification" of the country?

(Written for the Nanyang Special Edition at 1 a.m. on September 24th).

Woolen cloth transactions have been extremely prosperous recently. If it were not for the situation, business would surely be even more booming. The male and female colored woolen cloths required for autumn sales are being purchased by merchants from Hankou, Wenzhou, Hangzhou, Ningbo, Nanchang, Nanjing, Zhenjiang, and other ports. Those in the industry who have joined the association and registered with the customs are busy entertaining, transporting by post office and transport companies, and mostly trading in cash. Those who have not joined the association find business quite difficult.

Finance: Anglo-American-French Monetary Agreement Established; Standard Gold Buying Enthusiasm Dissipated; Yesterday Fell Another 1.10 Yuan 204

Yesterday, the gold market saw a decline of 1.10 yuan due to rumors of cooperation between the United Kingdom, the United States, and France in buying and selling gold, and of a large loan from the central government. At the beginning of the morning, overseas silver markets in the United Kingdom and the United States were flat, and the Montevideo forward silver price was unchanged. Exchange rates were stable. London spot gold was flat. The central bank's posted rates were flat in the United Kingdom and the United States, and the customs surtax was unchanged. The posted price for standard gold was still 1154 yuan. Reports that the U.S. Treasury Secretary announced an Anglo-American-French monetary agreement, a new type of gold standard, the main effect of which was to transfer the right to buy and sell gold from irresponsible speculators to the government, kept exchange rates from fluctuating excessively, and stabilized the gold market. Large investors were passive. The off-market pre-trading price retreated to 50.5 yuan due to the availability of Hengyu for sale. Qiasheng, Yongfuxing, and Yongfeng rose to about 3 yuan. The morning opened flat. After the opening, large investors' selling interest was still strong, and buyers lacked activity, gradually moving downstream. Although the HSBC Bank posted rates were flat in the United Kingdom and the United States, it had no impact. Whether the large loan between China and the United Kingdom was political or economic, it was ultimately unfavorable to the bulls. In addition, there were only two days of trading in the November contract, so there were many spot sellers in the market, so although the silver equalization tax was flat, it was still trending downward. Later, large investors repeatedly maintained the price at the bottom, and the market began to hover. The market situation for the morning is recorded below.

The morning opened at 1152.9 yuan, the same as the previous closing price. Qiafeng Yong sold, but Dadesheng, Fuyu, Fuxing, and Yong were still buying in multiple trades. Later, when HSBC Bank posted rates were flat in the United Kingdom and the United States, Qiafeng, Yong, Dadesheng, Tianfaqing, Fa Yongtong, and Fudeng sold in unison, retreating to 1.8 yuan. Qiafeng Yong bought at the bottom, rising to 2.2 yuan. However, Dadesheng, Jinfeng, and Yong continued to sell and gradually decline. The silver equalization tax was announced as unchanged, and the price fell to 1.1 yuan. Chunyuan, Yongyuan, Maoyong, Yida, Shengyuan, and Yonglai rose to 1.8 yuan. Fuyu, Daheng, and Dadesheng sold again, retreating to 1.2 yuan. Shenkang, Qiafeng, Yongyuan, and Maoyong bought at the bottom, and the price rose again to 1151.8 yuan at the afternoon close. After the close, Chengdai and others sold slightly, and the market weakened slightly.

The closing price, based on the central bank's standard gold price, was still posted at 1154 yuan, about 2 yuan more than the closing price. The month of registration was 1147 yuan, November was 1152 yuan, and the morning top-up price was 1147 yuan. The spot market was flat. Tianjin goods were priced at 13.75 yuan, the buying price of Hechi was 11.5 yuan, and the selling price of Hechi was 17 yuan. Shengyuan Yong sold 70 taels, and Tongfeng Heng sold more than 100 taels. It is predicted that the November contract will be rolled over to the December contract, and the bulls will pay about 2.5 yuan.

Trading in the market was limited. In summary, Qiafeng, Yongcheng, Datong, Hengwan, Xingfuxing, and Yongdadesheng, Shenkanghengyuding, Shengyuan, Yong, etc. were on the buying side, while Qingfa, Yongdaheng, Jinfeng, Yongda, Yongtong, Taichang, Chunyuan, Yongfuyu, and Tianfa, etc. were on the selling side.

It is difficult for the market to recover. The morning opened at 1152.9 yuan, the highest was 1152.9 yuan, the lowest was 1151.1 yuan, and the afternoon closed at 1151.8 yuan, with a fluctuation of 1.8 yuan. As a result, it continued to fall by 1.1 yuan. The total number of transactions in the morning was 2,499 bars.

The November lineup: the bulls are Qiafeng Yong with more than 1,400, Dachangxiang with less than 1,100, Yong with more than 800, Qingfayong and Hengchangyong each with more than 500, Fuda with five Changxiang each with more than 400, Wanxing Lifeng each with more than 300, Shenkang with more than 200, and Shunlida Shunbing Xingyishengyongxiang Fuyuhong Lidingkang each with more than 100. Securities: Bond Market Weak and Sluggish Again; Bullish Sentiment Gradually Apparent; Market Price More Likely to Fall Than Rise 206

Yesterday, the Shanghai Chinese Securities Exchange initially rose due to the British pound loan, but later weakened due to the strengthened situation. The market price seemed to be hovering, and the trend was showing signs of weakness. The loan between China and the United Kingdom was limited to goods. The chaos in eastern Sui had obviously come into contact, and the surface seemed to be a local problem, but in reality, it was related to the overall situation. In terms of type C bonds, it had never been benchmarked out at 60.05 yuan three times, and each time it turned small. The future may still return to the 60 yuan mark. The opening yesterday was entirely due to the news of the British pound loan. Buyers of No. 35 were particularly numerous, and the rest still sold at high prices, so although it rose by three or five cents, it did not seem strong. Sales of Nos. 11 and 14 were the most enthusiastic, and retail investors continued to buy in the second round. Nos. 4 and 6 sold quite a bit. Type E was slightly smaller, and the rest continued to do well by one or two cents. When the market opened in the afternoon, the market sentiment was already weak. It became known that the British pound loan was only for the supply of goods and did not benefit public bonds. The bulls of No. 35 turned to selling, and the selling of No. 32 was particularly enthusiastic. The market price unanimously turned down, small by five cents to one cent to two and a half cents. There were very few buyers at the close, and No. 14 continued to sell, again small by five cents to one cent to two cents. As a result, it still rose by one and a half cents to three and a half cents. The trend is that the short positions on the table have suffered losses, and those who short sell are becoming fewer and fewer, gradually forming a bullish sentiment, so the market price is more likely to fall than rise. The number of transactions totaled 6,535,000 yuan. The results of the rise and fall are compared in the table on the left (unit yuan, transaction unit hundred yuan).

Food: Flour Market Chaotic and Abnormal; Falling and Rising, Rising and Falling Again; Margin Requirement Increased to 500 Yuan Starting Today 207

Yesterday, the flour market was chaotic and abnormal in the morning after the opening. Each month's market was falling and rising, rising and falling again, which was the old trick of extreme speculators. When the opening price was set, Chicago foreign wheat was reported to be down by 12 cents, and the early districts abroad had received timely rain, so after the opening price, each month fell by two to three cents compared to the previous day. At the beginning of the second round of trading, the spot month was still down by one cent, but for November, the speculative bulls came out again and raised the price high. Starting from January, it rose by four or five cents compared to the initial round, exceeding the closing price of the previous day. The situation in the third round was even more chaotic. The spot month was raised as high as 3.65 yuan, and November was also up to 60 cents, but for the distant months, the bulls took the opportunity to release the margin, and the market calmed down. When the market opened in the afternoon, it was still tight at first, but later the buyers stopped and the large bulls released their positions one after another, causing the market to weaken and fall by three or four cents across the board. Looking at the current situation, if the foreign wheat market turns down, the market value has also reached its peak, and it should hover in place. In addition, the exchange will increase the margin requirement for both sides to 500 yuan starting this afternoon.

Reasons for the Decline in Wheat Futures: Authorities Maintain People's Food Supply…Many Bulls, Domestic and Foreign, Emerge; Foreign Wheat Prices are Slightly Lower…The Result Also Returns Seven or Eight Cents 208

Yesterday, the wheat futures market fell across the board in the morning because foreign wheat prices fell slightly, and it was rumored that the authorities had said that the high prices were affecting the people's food supply and that strict measures would be taken in the future, so the market calmed down at the opening, and the bulls inside and outside the industry released their positions one after another, and the situation took a sharp turn for the worse. Each month fell by three, six, and seven cents compared to the previous day. By the time the market opened in the afternoon, the market sentiment had become harmonious, and transactions were very smooth in each month, and the market returned by one or two cents. In the future, if exports are banned, the hoarders will inevitably be fearful, and the market may stabilize from then on. The current wheat market, due to customers selling back, the price of extra high-quality wheat has increased by one cent, and the price of medium-quality wheat has stabilized. Shandong wheat opened at 5.75 yuan, Yingzhou wheat at 5.7 yuan, Wuhe wheat at 5.65 yuan, second-class 63 cents, Yaowan wheat at 5.6 yuan, second-class 58 cents, Shahe wheat at 5.62 yuan, Yancheng wheat at 5.53 yuan, Hankou wheat at 4.75 yuan, Daorenqiao wheat at 5.3 yuan, second-class 25 cents, Guangshui wheat at 5.41 yuan, second-class 36 cents, and Zhumadian wheat at 5.55 yuan, Xianghe wheat at 5.2 yuan, and 5.1 yuan. Fuxin bought 3,000 bales, Fufeng bought 5,000 bales, and Shenda bought 2,000 bales.

Replenishing Short Positions in Sesame is Quite Strong; Soybean Sales Turn Sluggish 209

The recent sesame market needs to be observed in two ways: actual sales and offsetting short positions, so the trend is difficult to grasp for a while. Foreign companies' actual sales are not moving, and the market is only flat, but offsetting short positions is quite strong, and the source is not abundant, resulting in a lack of supply, so it still feels tight. Spot sales of raw sesame have Ningbo, Fuzhou, Shaoxing, and other places in this street purchasing thousands of bales of each variety of sesame. The market price is not much different from the previous market, and there may be a trend of rising greatly and falling back slightly in the future. Soybean sales have turned sluggish, and the demand from oil extraction plants has become stagnant. Yesterday, only 1,109 bales of Tancheng beans and 500 bales of Hankou vehicle beans were purchased. There were also fewer sales in Shantou, Fuzhou, this street, and other places. It is estimated that more than 1,200 bales of beans from all routes were traded, and the market price is temporarily high and stable, and the second-class is flat.

New Tinplate Greatly Lacking 210

Among the tinplate circulating in the market, the most common are Union Iron, Narrow Strip Iron, and Tag Iron. As for new iron of the genuine grade, the entire city feels a great lack. Therefore, printing factories and canneries all feel there is no stock to purchase. Prices are therefore gradually rising, such as single-linked [tinplate] at eighteen yuan and fifty cents, and double-linked opening at thirty-seven yuan and fifty cents (the above are prices for English, German, and Italian goods). As for domestic goods, the market price must be increased by two to three yuan, such as single-linked opening at twenty yuan and seventy-five cents, and double-linked at forty yuan. However, buyers are actively seeking [goods] from abroad.

Yesterday, Jardine Matheson and Ewo [洋行, foreign firms] sold four to five hundred barrels of zinc sheets, at a price of £18 5s per ton, an increase of 5 shillings compared to the previous price. It is reported that the latest overseas fixed price must be £18 17s, but due to the rapid price increase, many in the same industry are taking a wait-and-see attitude.

Popular Lectures

The Rise of Northern and Southern Merchants Competing for the Purchase of Ke Xian Rice 211

Yesterday, the Ke Xian rice arriving and being sold was both booming, with the market showing a firm stance. Subsequently, about 10,000 bags continued to arrive from various ports such as Xiangtan, Hankou, and Jiujiang. Although the Cantonese merchants had little appetite and Shantou was only clearing out inventory, with new transactions remaining hesitant, the demand from Northern ports suddenly surged. In addition to actively purchasing Hetao rice in the market, they also absorbed more than 3,000 bags of Xianggan machine-milled rice. The local appetite turned active. The Cantonese merchants also purchased more than 4,000 bags of Shashi and Hunan unpolished rice. Therefore, although the daily arrivals were robust, the market remained firm and brisk, with an estimated remaining stock of over 10,000 bags.

Tianjin Merchants Continue to Purchase Thick Xin Geng Rice 212

(South of Shanghai) Yesterday, the source of goods for various merchants still numbered about fifty, totaling over 10,000 piculs. Business at the local military ground was as usual. Fortunately, Tianjin merchants purchased nearly 1,000 bags of Thick Xin Geng rice, while merchants from Qingyan and other areas purchased 1,300 to 1,400 bags of Yaozhong rice, stabilizing the market. Daily prices remained unchanged. However, field rice, due to poor sales, dropped by one or two cents. Du Yang fried new rice and other varieties also did not see much fluctuation. Xin Yin Yuan Tong, thick and thin broken rice, slightly softened.

(North of Shanghai) Yesterday, the source of goods for various merchants at the river ports numbered about thirty-five or six. The market consumed various goods. Xin Geng rice and various pointed rice sold slightly better, while other goods remained sluggish. Market prices for high-quality Xin Geng rice were flat and weak, while medium and lower grades remained firm. Broken rice, Yang Du, port guest pointed rice prices remained stable. Yaozhong rice was scarce. Chen Bian Yuan high-quality goods remained firm, while medium and lower grades were slightly softer.

Silk and Tea: US and Japanese Prices Report Increases; Silk Transactions Revive in the Local Market 213

Yesterday, the overseas silk market gradually showed signs of recovery. Silk prices in both New York and Yokohama reported increases, significantly brightening the recent sluggish atmosphere. New York saw near and far term prices each rise by one and a half cents, while Yokohama spot prices rose by 10.50 yen and futures by 7 yen. As a result, silk trading in Shanghai gradually showed signs of activity. The quoted price from the French company was still considered too low, differing by about 50 yuan compared to the Shanghai market. The American company's silk prices were 630 yuan for self-branded B-grade silk and 640 yuan for Yangfan silk. If the overseas silk market can continue to strengthen slightly, American sales should improve. People in the local silk market are also optimistic. However, due to the inability of Yokohama silk prices to remain firm in the afternoon, the market sentiment felt hesitant again. The total trading volume for the day was only a hundred or so bales, with market prices generally rising slightly by three to five yuan compared to the previous day.

Sugar Market: Refined and Raw Sugar Plates Stable 214

Yesterday, the sugar market trend was stable. The association's planned plates, including No. 24 coarse sand white and Dongbai, remained unchanged. However, spot No. 9 and Dongbai were called up by five cents to 21.15 yuan. The local factory's refined white sugar was still called at the original price. Numbered goods from Chaozhou opened at over a hundred bags of Hainan foreign sugar, with the higher price at 16.2 yuan, followed by 15.9 yuan. Refined raw sugar from Songfa Zhuang, 72 bags, at 15.8 yuan; Qilin brand, 90 bags, at 15.4 yuan; and Huanggang Qing, 72 bags, with better color and luster, opened at 14.1 yuan.

The joint venture company yesterday held its second tender for Cantonese sugar this week, with a total fixed amount of 8,600 bags. Tender prices remained the same, with limited transactions. 415 bags of Shunde Factory's Five Sheep coarse white sugar were sold at 21.5 yuan; 40 bags from the Municipal New Factory at 21.3 yuan; 100 bags from Shantou Factory at 20.9 yuan; and 55 bags of medium sand white sugar at 19 yuan per bag.

Northern and Southern Goods: Quanzhou Dried Longan Production Reports Price Increase 215

Yesterday, the Quanzhou telegram reported that the dried longan in the production area had become tighter recently due to the purchase by foreign merchants. The upper grade only rose by about one yuan due to a larger quantity of goods, the middle grade rose by two yuan, and the lower grade, due to scarcity, saw a higher increase of three yuan. The goods opened by the trade associations have been sold off at fire-sale prices. For the highest grade, the businesses may still be losing money. Yesterday, the market slightly improved due to the increased production price, with the highest grade also rising by one yuan.

Guo Ziyi Meets the Uyghur Alone on Horseback 216

— Li Xi

During the early years of the Tang Dynasty in China, in the Yongtai period (1,172 years ago), in the ninth month, a traitorous general named Pugu Huai'en fabricated all sorts of lies and incited the Uyghur and Tubo, two foreign tribes, along with their accomplices from the Xiang and other tribes, totaling more than 300,000 people, to plunder in areas such as Jingzhou in our country. Their momentum was great, and they took the opportunity to directly attack Liquan and other places near the capital. The court was caught off guard and greatly shocked. Therefore, on one hand, they first took precautions, and on the other hand, they quickly called Guo Ziyi to gather troops in Jingyang to resist the enemy. However, Ziyi only had more than 10,000 soldiers at this time. Imagine using more than 10,000 soldiers to resist 300,000 soldiers; in reality, it was impossible. Furthermore, when Ziyi first arrived in Jingyang, he was already heavily surrounded by enemy soldiers. At this time, Ziyi's attitude was very calm, not panicked at all. He told all the generals to guard strictly and not to attack rashly. Coincidentally, at this critical moment, the traitorous general Pugu Huai'en died of a sudden illness, and the Uyghur and Tubo could not unite because of the struggle for power. Ziyi saw that the opportunity had arrived, so he immediately sent Li Guangxu as an envoy to meet the Uyghur.

Envoy Li took the order and ran straight to the enemy's Uyghur camp, met their leader—the chieftain, and said:

"I am sent by Guo Zhushi—to discuss with you, shall we join forces to fight the Tubo?"

The chieftain's face changed upon hearing this, and his attitude suddenly became awkward, as if he had developed a very heavy suspicion in his heart, but he still pretended to be calm and said:

"Is Duke Ling (the title by which Ziyi was respected by people at that time) really here? Are you really sent by Duke Ling? Hehe! Don't lie! Don't scare us with Duke Ling! If Duke Ling is really here, we must see him first to believe it."

Envoy Li listened to these words, then withdrew from the enemy camp and returned to his own camp to report in detail what he had said to the Uyghur chieftain.

Ziyi received the report and his courage increased a hundredfold, deciding to go alone to the enemy camp to meet the Uyghur commander. He immediately sent someone to arrange a meeting date with the enemy. At this time, his subordinates, both large and small generals, all came to dissuade him, saying:

"The Uyghur are barbarians, who do not value morality or understand integrity. You are a great general of the country, and your life is of utmost importance to the survival of the country. Be careful of your own body and do not risk going alone to meet them."

Ziyi said: "A person living in this world must value credibility and love the country. I have already made an agreement with the Uyghur, and I must abide by it; if the country is in distress, I must sacrifice myself to serve the country. Furthermore, if I don't go, it will only show that I, Guo Ziyi, am timid, weak, and incompetent. Now that such a large China is being oppressed by barbarians, who even dare to invade my country's vicinity with heavy troops, the most important thing at present is to promote the patriotic courage of us Chinese people. How can we show weakness? I am determined to go."

Seeing that Ziyi's determination to go was so firm that they could not stop him, the subordinates had no choice but to go with him and try to protect him. Unexpectedly, Ziyi stopped them again and said, "Let me go to see them alone. All of you cherish yourselves for the country, prepare for the worst, and avenge the country. Don't come with me." As soon as he finished speaking, he got on his horse, raised his whip, and galloped towards the Uyghur camp alone. The sentries along the road saw this situation and shouted to each other, "Duke Ling is here! Duke Ling is here!"

The Uyghur leader, Yaglu, received the news and was very surprised and suspicious. He led the leaders, big and small, prepared bows and arrows, and stood in front of the camp, waiting for Ziyi. After not much time, he saw that Ziyi had arrived. They put the arrows on the strings, ready to strike. Ziyi did not panic, approached the Uyghur camp, first took off his armor, put down his spears, and went straight in.

At this time, the Uyghur leaders, big and small, were shocked beyond measure, saying, "Duke Ling has really come." They immediately got off their horses, threw away their bows and arrows, and saluted Ziyi. Ziyi also got off his horse, greeted Yaglu, and said with a very gentle and solemn expression, "My China has always treated you extremely well, and you have always been extremely respectful to our country. Why did you only listen to Huai Ni's lies, lose the feelings between our two parties, and bring troops and horses deep into my country's vicinity, betraying China's consistent favor to you? Moreover, this Han traitor, Huai Ni, not only rebelled against the chaos, but even abandoned his old mother in order to rebel. What good is it for you to cooperate with such an unpatriotic and unfilial traitor? Now I am coming alone, because I value you and know that you can still listen. If you do not take these words to heart and even kill me, although I cannot resist again, my subordinates are not afraid of death, and they will definitely fight you to the death."

Yaglu listened to Ziyi's "righteous and stern" words and couldn't help but soften, saying, "Huai'en really deceived me. He said, 'The Khan (the foreign name for the Chinese emperor) has already passed away, and Duke Ling has already died.' I heard this lie, so I dared to come boldly. Now the situation is completely wrong. He is dead, and I have also understood. How dare we fight you again?"

Ziyi felt that the situation had become much smoother, knowing that the barbarians had always been ignorant of great righteousness and extremely greedy for small profits, and that the Uyghur were currently at odds with the Tubo, so he used the method of "using barbarians to control barbarians" to win him over, saying: "The Tubo's arrival this time is probably not for fighting, but for plundering property, right? If you don't believe me, think about how the livestock and horses they have plundered have been gathered together, and they are hundreds of miles long. This is clear evidence that they are determined to plunder. However, these many cattle, horses, and livestock are given to you by God. As long as we don't fight, listen to me and go to fight the Tubo together. After the victory, these many properties can be given to you. Think about it, is it worth it?"

Yaglu said: "We have already offended the superior country and Duke Ling by sending troops to the superior country after listening to the lies of the traitor Huai. Please forgive my sin! We will definitely help you." After the Uyghur finished speaking, they immediately took out wine and invited Duke Ling and all the association leaders to drink and pledge, and decided to do things according to the agreement, with no regrets.

On the other hand, the Tubo were still hesitant. Now that they heard that the two parties had already made an oath, knowing that their strength was too weak, they took advantage of the dark night and secretly fled, daring not to resist the superior country again.

When Duke Ling received this news, how could he let them go? He immediately arranged for the Uyghur troops to chase after them together. The captured and beheaded along the way were estimated to be more than 60,000 people. At the same time, he also tried to rescue the Chinese people who had been captured by them before. They were in a hurry to escape, so naturally they did not have time to move their property. Duke Ling took the property and sent it to the Uyghur as a reward. The Uyghur were grateful for the tolerance of the superior country, so they obediently withdrew their troops from China's territory.

From this battle, we can know how clever Ziyi's wit and how brave his courage were; and we can know that the encroachment of the barbarians is not terrible, as long as the whole country is united and studies methods to deal with them. What is terrible is only a sheet of loose sand, which is taken advantage of by the barbarians: By the time they are bullied, it is already too late to regret it. The Tang Dynasty praised him vigorously for this battle, and later generations praised him to the utmost. This is the story of "Guo Ziyi Meeting the Uyghur Alone on Horseback."

Faraday (Michael Faraday) 217

— Li Ren

— A Self-Taught Great Scientist —

Faraday was an English physicist and chemist. He invented inductive current, electrolysis laws, etc., and was a famous experimentalist in the scientific community. His origin was very humble. His achievements were entirely due to his hard work, perseverance, and constant learning, which enabled him to achieve complete success. The honor he received as a physicist and chemist was definitely not accidental.

Faraday was born in 1791. He was the third son of his father. His father was a blacksmith who could not work often due to his weak constitution, so the family was very poor. Faraday initially studied at a public school. At the age of thirteen, his father sent him to work in a bookstore, where he was assigned to be a newspaper delivery boy. After a year, he left the bookstore and became an apprentice in a bookbinding shop, with a term of seven years, graduating at the age of twenty-one. During these seven years of apprenticeship, whenever Faraday came across scientific books that he was binding, especially books on electricity, he would read and study them very carefully. Therefore, before long, he was making small glass bottles and tubes himself, and later he could even make electrical storage cylinders, although there were not many buyers. However, it was indeed an extremely difficult thing for a blacksmith's son to be able to make things and study electricity.

One day, Faraday heard that the scientist Mr. Tatum was giving a lecture on physics somewhere, held every seven days. The admission ticket cost twenty-five cents, which was too much for a bookbinding apprentice to afford. He went to discuss it with his brother Robert, who greatly supported his brother's aspirations and was willing to pay for the admission ticket each time. Faraday's first aspiration was successful because of his brother's help. At this time, a clerk skilled in drawing came to Faraday's shop, and he learned the technique of drawing unintentionally. Mr. Tatum's lectures were indeed well-deserved. Faraday also listened attentively and recorded everything the lecturer said, then transcribed it in regular script when he returned to the shop, eventually compiling it into four volumes, which he gave to his boss. Later, Faraday also heard the lectures of the chemist Sir Humphry Davy and was inspired to pursue chemistry.

In 1812, Faraday's bookbinding apprenticeship expired, and he wrote to Davy, saying that he was willing to learn chemistry from him, but Davy did not agree this time. Faraday could not get a mentor for the time being, so he self-studied Gatvanic. He initially used seven pieces of thin white lead, the size of half a copper coin, all plated with copper, and in the middle of each lead block, he used six layers of paper soaked in brine to protect it, to serve as a battery to electrolyze the essence of magnesium sulfate. Although Faraday did not gain much insight from trying to test profound electricity with such a shallow method, he himself had already felt the deep taste of chemistry.

Later, Faraday transferred to work in a bookbinding shop opened by a Frenchman. The shop owner was a reputable businessman in England. He had no children, and he discussed with Faraday that if he could work in the shop and never leave, he would give him the shop after his death. Faraday agreed, but the shop owner's temper was too bad, and Faraday was unwilling to be humiliated. Soon, he developed great ambitions.

One evening, Faraday suddenly received a letter from Davy, informing him that he would meet him in person tomorrow and had already agreed to find him a position in the academy. Faraday was overjoyed after reading the letter. The next morning, he went to the Royal Institution to visit Davy, who told him that he had found him a driver's position in the academy, with a salary of six yuan per week. The job was to clean the machines and deliver various supplies to the lecture stage during lectures, and there was nothing else to do. Faraday got this excellent job, so he resigned from the shop owner. From then on, he served in the Royal Institution, not only being able to hear valuable speeches often, but also being able to do various chemical experiments without spending money.

After entering the academy, Faraday decided on three principles for establishing himself: First, he believed that the academy was the place for him to settle down; second, he regarded books as good friends for further study; third, he strived to gain immortal fame. Based on these three principles, he succeeded in his great ambition.

Faraday experimented with various substances with Davy, experiencing many dangers. Initially, he invented the method of making sugar from turnips, and there was often a risk of explosion when combining dilute green gases. Several times, the glass mask covering his face was shattered, but fortunately, it did not damage his body. After seven months, Davy led him to visit France, Switzerland, Italy, and Mount Vesuvius. Whenever they encountered art academies and art schools, they would definitely go in to appreciate them. Faraday had both suffering and joy during the journey. The suffering was that he served Davy as a servant all the way, and he felt a lot of mental distress; the joy was that he, a young man who had never been outside the capital, was able to travel thousands of miles; and he was able to interact with famous scholars and writers of the time, which was truly the happiest thing in his life.

In the year that Faraday was twenty-four years old, he returned to England, at which time his annual salary had increased to 500 US dollars, and he was promoted to assistant instructor in the laboratory. When Davy was testing iodine gas and green gas, he also paid close attention. Davy created a safety lamp, which greatly benefited the workers in the mines, and Faraday's contribution was also not small. Faraday initially wrote six chapters of lectures, specifically discussing the affinity of matter and the method of defining and extracting homogeneity, which he presented publicly at the local natural history society, gaining much admiration from the audience. In the same year, he also wrote a chemical essay, detailing the viscosity of burning medicine (i.e., corrosive medicine). The following year, he wrote another six chapters of lectures, discussing coal gas and metal substances, and received much praise. After seven years, Faraday had graduated in chemistry. His writings totaled twenty-seven chapters, and there was also a book on the invention of steel alloys, as well as a chapter of lectures on two newly invented iodine-carbon mixtures, and the new quality of iodine-carbon light compounds that he had obtained from his experiments.

On June 12, 1812, Faraday married his lover Sarah Barnard. After marriage, he studied chemistry diligently and made more creations. After twenty years, his reputation had spread far and wide, and he was elected as a member of the Royal Society of England. He initially wrote twelve chapters of lectures on chemical refining techniques, followed by six chapters on chemical essence, and then six chapters on electromagnetism. In addition, he wrote books such as Elementary Knowledge, which he lectured on in various schools for as long as nineteen years. At the same time, five industrial societies in Woolwich hired him as the main lecturer, also for twenty years. Later, the government specially appointed him as an engineering consultant for the construction of lighthouses and the installation of buoys. When Faraday lectured, he often demonstrated in public to prove that what he said was true. Prince Albert also often led the Crown Prince to attend. Faraday wrote a total of one hundred and fifty-eight chemical treatises. Among them, the thirty chapters on electrical inventions were the best. Dr. Gladstone called these the masterpieces of England, which is indeed true.

Faraday's first discovery was that when extracting gasoline, he measured that the pressure of the gas could condense into a liquid. Following his father, he invented magnetically generated electricity and the method of conducting electricity through wires. Telegraphs and telephones originated from this.

After Faraday became famous, he was extremely filial to his mother, and he often remembered his deceased father, and he often said to people, "I like ironworkers very much, because they are very useful to the world, my father was also an ironworker, and I have never been ashamed of being the son of an ironworker." When Faraday was forty-nine years old, his mental strength suddenly declined. After his wife Sarah's advice, he went to Switzerland for treatment for four years before he was able to resume his normal experimental work.

Faraday worked in the laboratory, entering the academy every morning and going to bed at eleven o'clock in the evening. Except for meals every day, he never wasted a minute or a second of his precious time. When he got old and his body was truly weak, he stopped teaching. At that time, the whole world commemorated his achievements, and academic societies from all countries sent him medals and honored him as a director. French Emperor Napoleon III awarded him a responsibility. The Paris Exposition gave him the first prize medal, Queen Victoria specially hosted a banquet for him in the detached palace, and allowed her husband Prince Albert's request to specially award Faraday the first house of the government, which was truly glorious.

In the year that Faraday was seventy-one years old, his memory was almost completely lost; but he still executed all reports on lighthouses, motors, and steam engines himself.

On August 25, 1867, Faraday died in the chair of his study. His will was not to be buried in Westminster Abbey, mixed among the general dignitaries. He only wanted to be buried in Highgate Cemetery, and his will was not to erect a monument, but to insert a piece of white stone with the inscription of someone's tomb and the date of birth and death. Faraday was seventy-three years old when he died.

Publishing Industry

"Lin Qinnan" 218

— Jie Fei

The cold light shines, China Publishing

Mr. Lin Qinnan's writings once gave me a deep impression, especially *La Dame aux Camélias*, *Fu Zhang Lu*, and *Jinghua Bixue Lu*. My ability to roughly understand writing and write some classical Chinese is not without the benefit of Mr. Lin's enlightenment. His works, along with Mr. Liang Rengong's unrestrained and progressive writings and thoughts, had the same cultivating value for me.

Of course, times are advancing, and Mr. Lin's thoughts and writings are somewhat outdated. Even with this book, very few people borrow it from the library, which is clear evidence. But although Mr. Lin has been forgotten by others, he has never been forgotten by me. - Perhaps this is a bit of my stubbornness! Soon, I will still be asking for his *Mo Xia Zhuan*? - But here I can at least offer two points about Mr. Lin: first, his personality - a kind of Chinese "scholar-gentleman" personality - he "was young and willful, and people regarded him as mad, extremely passionate." Mr. Lin was a Confucian scholar, but also a [fierce/spirited person] - this is similar to Mr. Zhang Taiyan. - He had utmost affection, such as his sympathy - not limited to helping people of his time - his patriotism, his concern for the world, and his constant "crowing at dawn" - as Mr. Lin described himself - are all extremely commendable. And today's scholars rarely see such examples. In today's turbulent national situation, I personally long to promote this kind of "scholar-gentleman" category. Mr. Lin's contribution to translation and his lifelong diligence and loyalty are worthy of our admiration. He translated more than 140 foreign books - including short stories, no less than 200 - and his achievements in poetry and painting are also commendable. Even today, his translations such as *Fu Zhang Lu* and *Saxon Heroes* are still used as supplementary reading materials for middle school Chinese language classes, and no less than seven or eight types are included in the Wan You Wen Ku, and their influence, though changed, has not diminished.

What is regrettable is that since Mr. Lin passed away in 1923, in the past ten years, besides Mr. Zheng Zhenduo's article "Mr. Lin Qinnan" in *Fiction Monthly* and this book, there are almost no other memorial articles to be seen. The reason for this is that the old criticize his writing as being neither elegant nor completely colloquial - as Mr. Zhang Taiyan said - and that his writing conveyed morality but was irrelevant to new ideas - as Mr. Liang Rengong said - while the new blame him for translating second- and third-rate works and often losing the original meaning. Therefore, he is not appreciated by either side. It is sad that Mr. Lin's contributions have been obscured and not recognized!

This book's discussion is particularly fair and can trace Mr. Lin's intentions and actions, which is commendable. It is the only accurate record of Mr. Lin's life, ensuring that Mr. Lin's actions, conduct and writings will not be buried and forgotten, which is also commendable. However, I cannot help but comment: first, the structure of this book is too incomplete. Its table of contents is: 1. Brief Biography; 2. Thoughts and Enthusiasm; 3. Literary Criticism; 4. Translation; 5. Creation; 6. Literary Value and Achievements; 7. Conclusion. Listing literary criticism third is inappropriate in terms of sequence; also, the conclusion can be omitted. Second, this book is hastily written and its content is rather messy. For example, in the chapter on the brief biography, since the preface expresses dissatisfaction with Mr. Chen Yan's biography, then a complete and coherent biography should be written instead of just piecing together trivial remarks unrelated to his experience, which is negligent. Mr. Lin passed away only ten years ago, and his life and conduct are widely recorded in writings and oral accounts, which should be recorded and preserved to serve as material for understanding a person and discussing the world. Also, in the chapter on translation, many [blanks/dashes] are used in place of translated books. Since it is mentioned that *Fiction Monthly* has records, and *Fiction Monthly* is not a difficult book to obtain, it should be checked and written in to seek perfection. As for the conclusion, it is even more disjointed. There are also many repetitions and debatable arguments throughout, such as the claim that Mr. Lin's poetry was extremely successful, which I personally at least cannot agree with. - There are many such instances. Although it is not a hasty work - the author's preface was written ten years ago - it has many omissions and flaws.

I briefly record what I have seen, hoping that the author will make corrections and additions, collect more of his surviving works, and append a chronological biography to make it a perfect work. This is my wish.

The Doubting Antiquity School and the Social History School 219

— Yi Fu

In recent years, a very gratifying phenomenon in Chinese academia has been the willingness to put in substantial research into ancient history and to make substantial efforts to organize ancient academic thought. One school doubts antiquity, and the other is the school of social historians. Although their positions are different, they are unwilling to blindly believe in ancient history and ancient books. Instead, they re-evaluate them, use scientific and empirical methods to sweep away all previous outdated views, in order to open up a new path. This is completely the same.

The school of doubting antiquity can be traced back to Mr. Qian Xuantong, which can be seen from his personal abolition of his surname and his self-proclaimed name "Doubting Antiquity Xuantoong". He is immersed in hard work, and the most successful in recent times is Mr. Gu Jiegang.

In Beijing, there are organizations such as the Yu Gong Society and the Archeology Society. Their spirit and reality are worthy of infinite admiration.

The leader of the social history school is Mr. Guo Moruo, whose book "Research on Chinese Ancient Social History" is a famous masterpiece. Later, such as the *Reading Magazine* school, although their opinions differ from Mr. Guo's, they can also be classified into this category. And Tao Xisheng's founding of *Shi Huo* and his earnest efforts to organize work also reflect the excellent research spirit of social historians.

Regardless of Gu Jiegang's doubting antiquity school or Guo Moruo's social history school, both schools undoubtedly represent the progressive research spirit of Chinese scholars. They stand on a common front to overthrow the old learning, which is inevitably a necessary trend from all perspectives.

The doubting antiquity school shakes the halls of old national studies by determining the dates of the already completed classics and ancient books by the author; the social history school conducts various studies on Chinese culture, trying to emphasize the overthrow of unfounded speculations.

However, although these two schools are regarded as standing on the same front, their different beliefs and research methods often cause conflicts and resistance.

The former is a collection of scholars of old learning, while the latter has been nurtured by the emerging social sciences. At the same time, the social history school has repeatedly engaged in heated debates due to their different positions, while the doubting antiquity school is simply immersed in work. Although it is said that there are also differences of opinion and mutual disputes, they do not have theoretical goals, but rely on their own academic achievements, which is where the two differ.

Of course, scholarship flourishes through discussion. Because the two schools have different positions, there are often conflicts. The recent thesis by Mr. Ju is a manifestation of the doubting antiquity school attacking the social history school. Its title is "On the Origin of the Abdication Legend from the Mohist School," published in the first issue of the *Historical Studies Collection of the National Peking Research Institute*.

The so-called abdication, needless to say, refers to the story of Yao passing the throne to Shun, and Shun passing the throne to Yu, without passing it on to their sons, but rather to virtuous men. This is common knowledge for those who read Confucian books. Why has it become a major issue recently?

First, it is believed that the legend of Yao and Shun abdicating the throne, which is the most magnificent story in Confucianism, was entirely created by the Mohist school, which opposed Confucianism.

Second, Guo Moruo argued in "Research on Ancient Society" that the abdication of Tang and Yu was merely a misunderstanding of the clan chief election system during the matriarchal system.

Both of the above offer new criticisms of national studies and provide special insights, attempting to overthrow the empty and exaggerated legends of the past, which is the same goal. Gu's words are natural for criticizing old national studies, and there is no problem; but criticizing Guo's theory contains extremely complex problems.

Guo's "Research on Ancient Society" was a work from the era when the social history school emerged, so it is often the focus of criticism by later scholars. For example, even those belonging to the social history school were opposed by colleagues from *Reading Magazine* two years ago. Regarding issues such as matriarchal society and the marriage system, corrections to Guo's theory have continued to emerge from ancient historians in China and Japan, and Guo himself has also revised several points.

However, Gu's attack is not limited to Guo Moruo personally; it can be said to be directed at the entire social history school.

Originally, is the abdication legend a historical material passed down from an ancient social system? Gu believes that this is the Mohist school's advocacy of virtuousness, that is, a cultural work promoting egalitarianism. It originated from the Confucian school, was distorted by the Legalist school, and transformed by the Taoist school. He completely rejects treating this legend as historical material for ancient history. His arguments that the abdication legend originated from the Mohist school are roughly as follows:

In an era when the hereditary system existed rigidly, the fact that the emperor abdicated the throne to a commoner could not have occurred. In this era, as expressed in poems, books, or inscriptions on bronzes, there are mostly praises of the hereditary system. However, by the time of Confucius, the collapse of the hereditary system had already begun. Confucius himself was in a transitional era, troubled by the contradiction between the old system and new trends. Mencius' opposition to hereditary officials and Xunzi's and Gongyang Zhuan's opposition to hereditary succession are even more explicit. This opposition to the hereditary system became the fuse for the advocacy of virtuousness by the Mohist school. They regarded fishermen, cooks, and commoners as having the same abilities, and referred to high officials and emperors with the same titles. The Mohist school's ideal was a group that elected a leader to implement a democratic policy, and those who jointly advocated the abdication theory wanted to implement it within their own group. Once the Mohist theory became popular, the monarchs of the Warring States period also showed signs of wanting to implement abdication themselves. Mencius and Xunzi, both Confucian scholars, also adopted the Mohist school's advocacy of virtuousness. However, the abdication theory, which shook the position of the monarch, was still distorted and denied by the general public. For example, the Legalist school rejected Yao and Shun, who practiced abdication, as being contrary to the [relationship/principle] between ruler and minister; while the Taoist school extremely worshiped uncivilized people who did not accept abdication and despised Yao and Shun. Only in the Han Dynasty, when official learning was unified, did this abdication theory become a historical fact recorded in the *Yao Dian*, written by the gentle and orthodox Han people. (To be continued)
