Words of Conversation

Starting with Women's Longer Lifespan and Men's Shorter Lifespan 220

— Wu Ci

According to a recent study by Mr. Austin, Director of the U.S. Census Bureau, statistical methods prove that women live longer than men. He said that the average life expectancy of white women in the United States is 63 years, while the average life expectancy of men is 59 years. Mr. Austin's research is said to be based on the census statistics compiled in 1930. Whether this statistical method is accurate is naturally still a question, but assuming it is reliable, it would be more than 10 years longer than the average life expectancy of Americans surveyed in 1900 - 51 years for women and 48 years for men.

China's population still does not have accurate statistics, so the average life expectancy of men and women is naturally "out of the question." However, it can be speculated that it is unlikely to be longer than that of Americans. Years of natural disasters and man-made calamities, social exhaustion, and the difficulty of making a living often grind a strong "hero" into a thin and dying "sick man." In such circumstances, how can they not "die halfway"? Even relatively fortunate people are mostly licentious, indulging in wine and women, and living an unregulated life, which also self-destructs their natural lifespan.

This is just speaking generally. As for the lifespan between men and women, although no one has statistically analyzed it yet, it is the same as in the United States: women live longer than men. Why? Apart from the physiological differences between men and women, there are also great differences in the social environment they are exposed to. Just physiologically speaking, women over 50 seem to have less intense sexual desires, while men, even at 70 or 80, still want to take concubines. Although the reason for "taking a concubine" is to carry on the family line, if sexual desire is put aside, how will this "line" be carried on? Speaking of human affairs, China has always been a male-centered society. Although it is said that women's rights are high now, men still account for the absolute majority of the "pillars of society." Even within the family, women are in a subordinate position. Mental wear and tear and physical exertion are naturally greater for men than for women. Being able to live to 50 or 60 is already considered a long life, while it is not uncommon for women to live to 70 or 80. In the western suburbs of Shanghai, there is a [club/organization] called something, which held a weaving competition the other day. The first prize winner was a person called "Gai Meimei." Although the name sounds like a 16-year-old girl, she is already 80 years old.

Judging from this situation, the stronger the feudal forces, the greater the age difference between men and women. Although the United States is an advanced and civilized country, women's status is ultimately inferior to that of men, so women's average life expectancy is four years longer than that of men. In China, this number is roughly more than ten years. In a male-centered society, the lifespan of men is so short, which is really not a good phenomenon.

But the problem is not the difference between men and women, but how to increase the average age of human beings.

People always have a desire to survive. The methods of health preservation lie in using all human wisdom to fight against nature. The most important thing is the progress of medicine and the improvement of living standards. With advanced medicine, diseases that shorten human life will have no way to run rampant, and raising the standard of living will further eliminate the occurrence of diseases as much as possible. But although humans have such wisdom, the inferior nature of killing each other can never be eradicated. So on the one hand, there are facilities to protect health, and on the other hand, there are weapons to manufacture mutual killing. If mankind is to be destroyed, the road to destruction is one we walk ourselves!

Heng Xu 221

— Yu Lu

It's morning. The city is awakened by a few workers and vendors at the early market, and the stupid fellows sweeping the streets.

Now it's a little past 5 a.m. In the early autumn of the South, at this time, the sky already has a white, misty silver light, shining on the newly laid black asphalt road. Two or three rickshaw pullers on the "night shift," dozing off, use their two powerful arms to press on the rickshaw pole with no urgency, dragging their weary steps forward. From time to time, two or three cars pass swiftly and silently, startling them from their feigned sleep. They immediately remember to hurry to "Xiti" to pick up the early ferry. Therefore, they sing "Half a chicken, a pot of Yong Liwei..." and pull the rickshaws south.

At this time, a group of "buyers" of old goods, each carrying a full load of old goods on a shoulder pole, turn a corner from the new road of "Xia Jiupu" and walk west. They walk very neatly and quietly, as if afraid of disturbing anyone in the early morning.

They don't walk far before they encounter several "fellows." When they meet acquaintances, they greet each other as usual:

"Good morning! Good business?"

"Good morning," they answer politely, and then it's the usual line that has become common in recent years: "Not good! Business is more difficult these past few years than before!"

This kind of life is already customary for them. At most every other day, they have to rush to "Heng Xu" early in the morning to sell off the goods they've collected, otherwise the capital will be tied up and they won't be able to turn around. Then even selling the ancestral fields won't be enough to cover the losses.

Heng Xu is their designated meeting place. Every day, before it's fully light, they do buying and selling business, and then disperse when it gets light. This is a very strange custom, very much like the true saying that "old goods can't see the light." Therefore, the history of this Heng Xu can be considered quite old in this city. Although it has been banned several times, it's nothing more than changing locations and starting over.

The current location is in front of a dark [temple/shrine] at "Xilai Chudi."

The lights are still on, and heads are surging under the ghostly lights. The sounds of bargaining are replaced by fingers and abacus beads. The scene is like a clandestine secret business. A new team of "fellows" joins in, and the situation becomes lively. The waving of hands also increases in power. Buyers and sellers are very skilled in speaking many of the terms of the trade. This one is haggling to "squeeze up!" The other side, the "customer," is unwilling to pay, and only offers one! "Three seven qian and two!" Although the price difference is too great, neither side is willing to give in, not even half a "dou ling."...

"Country bumpkin, don't be so stubborn, sell it and you'll lighten your shoulders, saving yourself the trouble of carrying it back and forth."

Page 20

"Those who know the goods buy the goods. This is not like selling antiques at "Shuangmen Di," the prices are honest, how can the difference be so great!"

"Alright, alright! I'll add you two fen and four, sell it or don't, it's up to you!"

"Business depends on repeat customers! Good, good, good!"

Thus, another item changes hands in the dark.

Of course, there are also people arguing here. Like some "outsiders" who come to Heng Xu for the first time, they are unfamiliar with the trade and don't know what's going on. "The boat's head is panicked by ghosts, the boat's tail is panicked by thieves!" They want to be greedy for cheap, but they are also afraid of being tricked. So, you say one thing, I say another, and everyone starts shouting and cursing.

The sky is slowly being dyed half red. The light of the lamps loses its flame under the sunlight, and Heng Xu also appears desolate. The crowded people all disperse at once. When dawn returns, the square returns to silence. The ground is littered with remnants, and another morning begins to arrive in the human world.

In people's memory, Heng Xu occupies a very small place. If you are from a [wealthy/urban] family, even if you are an old Guangzhou person, you may not know about it.

(Note) Xidi, Xia Jiupu, Xilai Chudi, and Shuangmen Di are all place names. "Zha zhu" means five, referring to "five yuan" here. Qi Qian Er is "one yuan". "Dou Ling" is half a jiao (cent). "Er fen si" is "three fen" one jiao (cent). "Selling antiques at Shuangmen Di" is a common saying, meaning "asking for a high price."

People Who Are Strangers to Their Motherland 222

— Lan Pei

——Record of a Village Trip.

"Are there bandits everywhere in Tangshan?"

My cousin curiously asked me for some news about China. Her family and the friends around her had never mentioned China to her. Occasionally, she could see a small piece of information about China in the Malay newspapers, which vaguely made her realize that China was indeed a barbaric place filled with bandits.

"No--it's a good place! Bandits, that's just something in the deep mountains. Aren't there bandits in Kalihyu (a place name in Malaysia)? In short, Tangshan is not as scary a place as you know it. If you've ever been there, you'll be infinitely amazed! Maybe you won't want to come back, like me. Haven't I only returned once in three years?" I tried my best to explain.

My cousin didn't believe it, and smiled slyly: "Tangshan, the land of sweet potatoes (Note 1)!"

"Sweet potatoes may not be a good thing to eat. However, there are also Western-style houses in Tangshan, even more magnificent than those here. Haven't you seen photos? Then you must have seen movies, that's Tangshan!"

"Oh, that's right," my cousin laughed loudly. "That's Shanghai. Do you think I don't know that!"

I was almost a little annoyed. I hadn't expected that my cousin would be so unfamiliar with her motherland. Not understanding the situation of the motherland is understandable, but not even recognizing the most important places in the motherland is simply too unreasonable. "Overseas Chinese students, Dutch education!" I scolded in Chinese, indignantly.

"Shanghai is Tangshan! Have you read world geography? There's a page in there that says this. Shanghai, one of the world's largest cities, the economic and cultural center of China. -- Also, Guangzhou, you know that, right? Beijing, Tianjin, are all better than here, cars--whatever you say, everything is available. There's just one thing, there aren't people wearing "sarongs" like you."

"Maybe Shanghai is Tangshan, but--"

My cousin laughed again, as if this was an interesting thing.

"No way," I said to myself. "Like this, what can be done. She simply doesn't recognize herself as Chinese anymore. They, those thousands upon thousands of overseas Chinese students who are educated by the Dutch." I couldn't help but shout loudly: "No way, you can't look down on Tangshan like that, you're still Chinese after all--can you say you're Dutch?"

"Oh, I didn't say I was Dutch--I'll still ask you nicely: Cousin, didn't you say that Shanghai is Tangshan? So: is Shanghai really like in the movies?"

"Uh--of course; hey, I didn't say that Shanghai is Tangshan, that's really like that--that's really funny! For you to say that."

I began to feel the power of the Dutch enslaving education system.

"People who are strangers to their motherland!"

I said quietly, indignantly.

Note: "People who eat sweet potatoes" is an idiom, meaning clumsy.

Signing 223

— Chuan Chuan

—Life Record—

The urgent shaking of the bobbins and the loud roaring of the machines in the workshop could not prevent her thoughts. While watching the yarn transfer from the small bobbin to the large one, followed by a thread breakage, she was planning for Xing's future. When she thought of sweet moments, her heart smiled.

Although she would still be unable to leave the factory life, unable to avoid standing in front of the machines for twelve hours every day, breathing in dust and cotton fibers, perhaps, the "foreman" of another factory would not be as hateful as the current one. Perhaps, the wages at another factory would be a little higher. These things didn't need to be worried about for now. As long as she wasn't sold by her heartless mother to a forty-eight-year-old tycoon as a concubine, she would be happy enough.

She wanted to live with him—her lover—in a small room in Yangshupu. Both of them would work at the same time and eat at the same table. No one would scold her, no one would take all of her wages, preventing her from buying even a slightly nicer dress.

In her sweet fantasies, time flew by quickly. In the blink of an eye, the red light turned on, and the workers turned off their machines and rushed to the dining hall together. When she came back, she found the "Number One," and told her that she wanted to sign out. The "Number One" was a very kind old woman, and she agreed to her request without asking any questions, and even offered to find the foreman to sign for her.

At two o'clock in the morning, she bid farewell to her little sisters in the workshop, especially saying a few words of gratitude to the "Number One." With the paper signed by the foreman in her pocket, she brushed off the cotton fibers on her head and clothes, and stepped into the personnel department.

She only glanced at the red-faced section chief, then quickly lowered her head and said softly,

"Sir, I'm signing out." At the same time, she handed the paper signed by the foreman to him.

"Quitting to work at another factory?" The voice sounded like it was bursting out of a tightly closed bottle.

"No!" she quickly said, glancing at him again.

His hands were flipping through a thick book, but his eagle-like eyes were glancing at her sideways. His two blood-red, thick lips were crooked, and he softened his voice a little:

"Why is that?"

"I'm not doing it anymore," she said softly.

"Hmph! Not doing it anymore? You're not allowed to sign out." His voice became rough again, and he lowered his head, focusing on the book.

Her face turned red. She wanted to argue with him that quitting was her freedom, but she immediately softened, thinking that doing so would not end well, and her wages would definitely be confiscated. She had to lower her voice and say gently,

"Sir, I want to..." She couldn't go on, she couldn't bring herself to say it.

"What? Getting married?"

She had to nod.

"Marrying who?" The section chief propped his hands on the table, leaning on one shoulder, and asked.

"What does it matter to you who I marry?" she couldn't help thinking. But for the sake of the money, she had to endure and answer.

The section chief urged her again, and she had to answer:

"Zhou Zhiying."

"Hmph, is that the yarn weigher in the fine yarn workshop? You're having an affair, you're not allowed to sign out!"

She almost cried. She wanted to grab him and slap him hard a few times, but she endured it. However, her tone already carried resentment.

"Sir, I'm signing out, give me my wages!"

The section chief's eyes were back on the book, and he said fiercely:

"Go back, call someone from your family to prove it, if you lie, your wages will be confiscated! Get out now!"

Every muscle in her body was twitching. She bit her lip, glared at him with all her might, took the gate pass he had written, and stormed out of the room in anger.

At the factory gate, Zhou Zhiying was waiting for her. Seeing her mournful face, he was stunned and dropped his smile.

"He won't let me sign out, what do you think we should do? Adding our wages together, I could get twelve yuan, now... now..." She cried.

The other's response was a long sigh of disappointment.

"What about you?" she asked him, holding back her tears.

"I signed out and got thirteen yuan."

"Why did he let you sign out?"

"If I didn't sign out myself, he would have fired me anyway. Don't you see that the yarn weighers in other workshops have all been replaced with female workers?"

The two of them involuntarily turned their eyes to the tall red factory building, casting one last angry look at the factory that had bound them for five years.

The Crime

"Yes, since you are a human, you should live on, but what if you can't live on..."

Yu Shouguang is someone who wants to live on but can't. He has no food to eat, no place to live, so he has no way to live on. He thinks of committing suicide... However, he also feels afraid of death, and he has to think of a comfortable way to die. So he stole the felt from the inn to pawn for one yuan and two mao, and he decided to go to the pharmacy to buy "Over-the-Mountain Cyanide"—a kind of poison—to commit suicide. However, the snobbish pharmacy owner saw his ragged appearance and suspected that he was buying it to kill someone, so he wouldn't sell it to him.

Yu Shouguang, who couldn't even get the freedom to seek death, was extremely angry. He had a conflict with the pharmacy owner and broke the store's glass cabinet. He was taken to the police station to be convicted.

The law is also a tool for the rulers to be accomplices. What crime do you think they will convict him of?

Suzhou Ballad 226

Cao Xiaoying's Yu Qing Ting

Central West (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:30 PM

Opening "New Oriole Worships the Moon"

The jade sky is dust-free, with a round moon. Hong Niang invites the young lady to the east building. Lightly moving lotus steps down the high building, seeing the flowers and moonlight evenly divided. Flowers have a clear fragrance and the moon has shade. Miss, the moon is bright, no need for flower lanterns, the lanterns pale in comparison to the moon. Hong Niang, looking at flowers under the moon brings wealth and honor, appreciating the moon before flowers brings good spirits. Flower souls invite moon spirits, moon spirits charm flower souls. Flowers fill the spring garden, the moon fills the forest. They, step through flowers under the moon, already arrived at the flower and moon forest's four-sided hall. Hong Niang is, the incense table arranged under the flowers and moon. I hope that the flower god and moon sister will feel my sincerity. Miss is, the first stick of incense inserted in the burner, bowing and kneeling on the cushion. Swallows and orioles sing a pious prayer, hoping the gods will hear my plea. Alas, my father passed away from illness and returned to the spring road, I have not yet fulfilled my filial duty. The second stick of incense inserted with both hands, may it protect my mother's longevity and fortune, may she be as evergreen as the pine and cypress of Nanshan. Miss is, kowtowing deeply, pondering again. The third stick of incense burned with tears, only there is no place to voice ten thousand idle sorrows, a belly full of grievances cannot be expressed. Therefore, silently expressing sincerity. Resenting only, my father's confused words during his illness, saying that he wants to marry into the Zheng family, relatives of the maternal side. The two families are originally one family. I am ashamed to tell my mother, hoping the gods will show my white-haired parent in a dream. Miss is, silently telling the things in her heart, who knows she has leaked two or three points. Spring scenery is always annoying.

Chen Lianqing and Qi Lianfang's Small Coin

Opening "Dream of the Red Chamber: Qin Keqing"

The beautiful flower branch Qin Keqing, has a soft nature unparalleled in the world. She is, from a poor Qin family girl, marrying into a noble family like a deep sea. Glad only, her husband Jin Gui is somewhat comforting. Resenting only, her delicate body is often ill and groaning. But seeing her, knowing and befriending Wang Xifeng, extraordinarily pitiful to Shi Taijun. She is, ranked as a Golden Hairpin as an adopted daughter, causing her, flower face to wither, pitifully. Rong Ge'er, only knows to steal jade and incense, ignoring Jin Min's body illness. Once remembered, the brocade tent confuses the dream, the phantom land teases Shen Ying. To this day, the case is difficult to recognize, feeling that the first crime should be blamed on Hua Xiren. Unexpectedly, the fragrant soul easily breaks, how can one bear the jade breaking and the pearl sinking. Wang Xifeng, meets in a dream and startles from a dream, cloud board conveys the news to the whole house. Most painfully, the family of gods is too hasty, returning to Penglai is the cause of the past. I am, writing this opening as a subtle expression.

Flowery World

Ice and snow. Morning and night. The east wind moves. Spring is here. Flowers blossom everywhere, layer upon layer. Mornings reflect the clouds and rosy light. Nights accompany the gentle breeze and bright moon. Attracting swallows and orioles, startling bees and butterflies. Enticing lovers' joy, provoking laborers' farewell. Just a fleeting flowery world. Take advantage and don't worry about the rich buying and the poor owing.

Everyone loves. Fresh flowers and tender leaves. Especially those brothers and sisters. Even those younger brothers and sisters. Even those older grandmothers and grandfathers. Bamboo huts outside the forest. Tall buildings and long streets in the metropolis. Who can divide the rich and poor. Who can discern the elegant and vulgar. Some people fear spring's old age and flying flowers. Some worry about autumn's withered and fallen leaves. Red flowers bloom and white flowers fade continuously throughout the year. No time to manage so many things.

Movie News

The Male and Female Leads of "Madame" 229

After re-screening "Aquatic Rhapsody" for two days, the Nanjing Grand Theater will continue to screen MGM's blockbuster "Madame". The film stars the runaway bride Barbara Stanwyck and the handsome British envoy Robert Taylor. The film tells the story of a love triangle between a pair of brothers and a woman. Robert Taylor has been enthusiastically loved by hundreds of millions of viewers since starring in "Broadway Melody of 1936", and is considered a goddess by women. For "Madame," the company originally intended to have Qin Hen Haruo as the female lead, but after learning that Robert Taylor and Barbara Stanwyck were very close, they appointed Barbara Stanwyck as the female lead, so that the audience could see the more realistic love scenes on the screen. The film is directed by Van Dyke, the director of "San Francisco," whose masterful skills add a lot of color to the film.

Guotai Screens "Girl's Dormitory" 230

When Shown at the Los Angeles Theater in the United States, Audiences Reached 150,000 in One Week

The latest production of 20th Century Fox, "Girl's Dormitory", is scheduled to be shown at the Guotai Grand Theater starting today (Thursday). The story of the film tells about a girls' school with strict rules on the Alps. Many daughters of the upper class in Europe are sent to study here, but food and sex are human nature. These young girls are just beginning to feel love and are eager to have something to rely on, so the living trick of teacher-student love occurs. The plot is tortuous and bizarre, and the performance describes the girls' passionate emotions. It can be said to be meticulous. The main characters are Herbert Marshall, Ruth Chatterton, and the newly discovered French beauty star Simone Simon. It is worth mentioning that Simone Simon's acting skills, although this is her first work in Hollywood, have already made her one of the first-class stars in the United States. No one in the country does not praise her. It is heard that when the film premiered at the Los Angeles Theater in the United States, the audience reached 150,000 in one week. We can imagine the grand occasion at that time.

Minxin Telecommunications 231

"New Humanity" will start filming soon, and director Chu Wancang will lead the photography team to Xuzhou and Qingjiangpu to capture location shots.

Li Keng's younger brother, Li Xi, who was born not long ago, once appeared in "Life". Recently, he will show his skills again in "New Humanity", playing the role of the young son. In the silent "New Humanity", Li Keng originally played this role alone, and became famous in one fell swoop. This time, Li Xi and Li Keng will play the role separately, which may create a new child star for the Chinese film industry.

Ms. Lin Chuchu has fully recovered after giving birth and will soon appear in "The Gate of Flesh and Spirit".

Xiao Ying plays the main character in "The Gate of Flesh and Spirit". In the first half of the film, he plays a dim-witted alcoholic gambler, and in the second half, he transforms into a serious, kind, and self-sacrificing figure. He will set a new record in Chinese actors' acting skills.

Ge Youzhi and Li Keng will have extremely important performances in "The Gate of Flesh and Spirit", and are currently practicing carefully.

Shi Shipan is in charge of photography for "New Humanity".

Wen Rong plays a thief and gambling den owner in "The Gate of Flesh and Spirit".

"Mother's Love" will be premiered at the Jincheng Grand Theater in Shanghai at the end of this month. The film has achieved excellent results in its premiere in Pingjin, and Minxin colleagues held a meeting to celebrate it.

"Venus" Issue 7 Published 232

The seventh issue of the Tianjin Venus Pictorial has been transported from Tianjin to Shanghai. All major bookstores and newsstands in the local area are selling it. Buyers are very enthusiastic. The entire issue is printed on heavy-duty wood-free paper, and the printing is excellent. Each issue is sold for only 15 cents. The content is divided into literature, drama, film, comics, and epigraphy and calligraphy. It is very rich. Submissions are welcome. Correspondence address: No. 37, Jianye West Lane, Fuli Road.
